        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 6pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt">At September 29, 2009, the number of shares outstanding of the registrant&rsquo;s common stock, $0.0001 par value (the only class of voting stock), was 50,265,000.</font></p>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="center">PART I</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><a name="A3"></a><a name="itemone">ITEM 1.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;BUSINESS</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>As used herein the terms &ldquo;</i><i>Waste to Energy</i><i>&rdquo;</i> <i>&ldquo;we,&rdquo;</i> <i>&ldquo;our,&rdquo;</i> <i>&ldquo;us,&rdquo;</i> <i>&ldquo;it,&rdquo;</i> <i>and &ldquo;its&rdquo;</i> <i>refer to Waste to Energy Group Inc. unless context indicates otherwise.</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="center">Corporate History</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy Group Inc., was incorporated in the State of Nevada on June 27, 2006 under the name &ldquo;Your Digital Memories Inc.&rdquo; We are a development stage company that has not generated revenue since inception.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy, a wholly-owned subsidiary of Your Digital Memories Inc., was incorporated in the state of Nevada on August 13, 2008. Waste to Energy and Your Digital Memories Inc., entered into an Agreement and Plan of Merger on August 14, 2008. The board of directors of Waste to Energy and Your Digital Memories Inc., deemed it advisable and in the best interests of their respective
        companies and shareholders that Waste to Energy be merged with and into Your Digital Memories Inc., with Your Digital Memories Inc., remaining as the surviving corporation under the name &ldquo;Waste to Energy Group Inc.&rdquo;<br>
        <br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        <br>
        Since incorporation, we have shifted our focus from developing and offering software products to the creation of interactive photo slideshow products and most recently to renewable energy development. On September 8, 2008 we entered into a memorandum of understanding to acquire Waste to Energy Group LLC pursuant to a share exchange. Waste to Energy Group LLC was involved proprietary waste to energy conversion technology. However, on completing a thorough due diligence inquiry into the
        opportunity presented by this technology, the decision was made to abandon the prospective transaction.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Since the abandonment of the agreement with Waste to Energy Group LLC we have had limited operations. Our sole executive officer and director devotes limited time and attention to our affairs.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Our office is located at 2829 Bird Avenue, Suite 12, Miami Florida, 33133 and our telephone number is (786) 206-5368. Our registered agent is Island Stock Transfer, 100 Second Avenue South, Suite 300 N, St Petersburg, Florida. 33701.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Waste to Energy is listed on the Over the Counter Bulletin Board under the symbol &ldquo;WTEG&rdquo;.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="center"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="justify"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">is in the process of</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">considering business opportunities for development, merger or acquisition that might create value for its shareholders.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="justify"><i><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Selection of a Business<br>
        &nbsp; </font></i></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Management has adopted a conservative policy of seeking opportunities that it considers to be of exceptional quality. Therefore, we may have to wait some time before consummating a suitable transaction. Management recognizes that the higher the standards it imposes upon us, the greater may be its competitive disadvantage when vying with other
        acquiring interests or entities.</font><br>
        </p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">3</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">does not intend to restrict its consideration to any particular business or industry segment, though management intends to continue its focus on opportunities related to natural resources. Due to our lack of financial resources, the scope and number of suitable business ventures is limited. We
        are therefore most likely to participate in a single business venture. Accordingly, Waste to Energy will not be able to diversify and will be limited to one development, merger or acquisition. The lack of diversification will prevent us from offsetting losses from one business opportunity against profits from another.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">The decision to participate in a specific business opportunity will be made upon management&rsquo;s analysis of the quality of the opportunity&rsquo;s management and personnel, the anticipated acceptability of products or marketing concepts, the merit of technological changes and numerous other factors which are difficult, if not impossible, to
        analyze through the application of any objective criteria. Further, it is anticipated that the historical operations of a specific venture may not necessarily be indicative of the potential for the future because of the necessity to substantially shift a marketing approach, expand operations, change product emphasis, change or substantially augment management, or</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">make other changes. Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">will be
        partially dependent upon the management of any given business opportunity to identify such problems and to implement, or be primarily responsible for the implementation of required changes.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Since we may participate in a business opportunity with a newly organized business or with a business which is entering a new phase of growth, it should be emphasized that Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">may incur risk due to the failure of the target&rsquo;s management to have proven its abilities or effectiveness, or the
        failure to establish a market for the target&rsquo;s products or services, or the failure to realize profits.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">will not acquire or merge with any company for which audited financial statements cannot be obtained. Management anticipates that any opportunity in which we participate will present certain risks. Many of these risks cannot be adequately identified prior to selection of a specific opportunity.
        Our shareholders must therefore depend on the ability of management to identify and evaluate such risks. Further, in the case of some of the opportunities available to us, it may be anticipated that some of such opportunities are yet to develop as going concerns or that some of such opportunities are in the development stage in that same have not generated significant revenues from principal business activities prior to our participation.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left"><i>Acquisition of Business</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Implementation of a structure for any particular business acquisition may involve a merger, consolidation, reorganization, joint venture, franchise or licensing agreement with another corporation or entity. Waste to Energy may also purchase stock or assets of an existing business. On the completion of a transaction, it is possible that our present management and shareholders would not remain
        in control of Waste to Energy. Further, our sole officer and director may, as part of the terms of any transaction, resign, to be replaced by new officers and directors without a vote of our shareholders.</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">We anticipate that any securities issued in any such reorganization would be issued in reliance on exemptions from registration under applicable federal and state securities laws. However, in certain circumstances, as a negotiated element of any transaction, Waste to Energy may agree to register securities either at the time a transaction is consummated, under certain conditions, or at a
        specified time thereafter. The issuance of substantial additional securities and their potential sale into any trading market may have a depressive effect on such market.</p>

        <p></p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">4</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">While the actual terms of a transaction to which Waste to Energy may be a party cannot be predicted, it may be expected that the parties to a business transaction will find it desirable to avoid the creation of a taxable event and thereby structure the acquisition in a so called &ldquo;tax-free&rdquo; reorganization under Section 368(a)(1) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended (the
        &ldquo;Code&rdquo;). In order to obtain tax-free treatment under the Code, it may be necessary for the owners of the acquired business to own 80% or more of the voting stock of the surviving entity. In such event, our shareholders would retain less than 20% of the issued and outstanding shares of the surviving entity, which could result in significant dilution in the equity of such shareholders.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Our due diligence process will require that management meet personally with the personnel involved in any given transaction, visit and inspect material facilities, obtain independent analysis or verification of the information provided, check references for management and key persons, and take other reasonable investigative measures, to the extent of our limited financial resources and
        management expertise.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">The manner in which we participate in an opportunity will depend on the nature of the opportunity, the respective needs and desires of Waste to Energy and other parties, the management of the opportunity, and the our relative negotiating strengths. Negotiations that involve mergers or acquisitions will focus on the percentage of Waste to Energy that the target company shareholders would
        acquire in exchange for their shareholdings in the target company. Depending upon, among other things, the target company&rsquo;s assets and liabilities, our shareholders will in all likelihood hold a lesser percentage ownership interest in Waste to Energy following any merger or acquisition. The percentage ownership may be subject to significant reduction in the event Waste to Energy acquires a target company with substantial assets. Any merger or acquisition effected by Waste to
        Energy can be expected to have a significant dilutive effect on the percentage of shares held by our current shareholders.</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><i><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Operation of Business after Acquisition</font></i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy&rsquo;s operation following its merger or acquisition of a business will be dependent on the nature of the business and the interest acquired. We are unable to determine at this time whether Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">will be in control of the business or whether present management will be in control
        following the acquisition. We may expect that any future business will present various challenges that cannot be predicted at the present time.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Competition</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">We will be involved in intense competition with other business entities to obtain a suitable business opportunity many of which competitors will have a considerable edge over us by virtue of their stronger financial resources and prior experience in business.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Marketability</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">As we currently are not involved in selling products or services, there can be no assurance that we will be successful in marketing any such products or services or whether a market will develop.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Patents, Trademarks, Licenses,</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Franchises, Concessions, Royalty Agreements and Labor Contracts</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">We currently have no patents, trademarks, licenses, franchises, concessions, royalty agreements or labour contracts.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">5</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Governmental and Environmental Regulation</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">cannot anticipate the government regulations, if any, to which it may be subject until it has acquired an interest in a business. The use of assets to conduct a business that Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">may acquire could subject it
        to environmental, public health and safety, land use, trade, or other governmental regulations and state or local taxation. Our selection of a business in which to acquire an interest will include an effort to ascertain, to the extent of the limited resources of Waste to Energy, the effects of any government regulation on any</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">prospective business. However, in certain circumstances, such as the acquisition of an interest in a new or start-up business
        activity, it may not be possible to predict with any degree of accuracy the impact of government regulation.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Research and Development</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="justify"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">No expenditures were made on research and development activities during either of the last two fiscal years.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Employees</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left">As of September 29, 2009 we have two consultants including one executive officer who works on a part-time basis. We use additional consultants, attorneys, and accountants as necessary to assist in the development of our business.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><a name="itemonea"></a></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><a name="A6"></a>ITEM 1A.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;RISK FACTORS</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy&rsquo;s operations and securities are subject to a number of risks. Below we have identified and discussed the material risks that we are likely to face. Should any of the following risks occur, they will adversely affect our business, financial condition, and/or results of operations as well as the future trading price and/or the
        value of our securities.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left"><i>W</i><i>e have a history of significant operating losses and such losses may continue in the future.</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left">Waste to Energy incurred net losses of $411,434 for the period from June 27, 2006 (inception) to the year ending May 31, 2009. At the year ending May 31, 2009 we had a working capital deficit of $344,089 and stockholders&rsquo; deficit of $328,242.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left"><i>Waste to Energy</i><i>&rsquo;s limited financial resources cast severe doubt on our ability to acquire</i> <i>or develop a revenue producing business.</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left">Our future operation is dependent on our ability to acquire or develop a revenue producing business. However, the prospect of such an acquisition is doubtful due to Waste to Energy&rsquo;s limited financial resources which limitation may act as a deterrent in future negotiations with prospective acquisition, merger or development candidates. Should we be unable to improve our
        financial condition through debt or equity offerings our ability to acquire or develop a revenue producing business will be severely limited to the extent that Waste to Energy will, in all likelihood, be forced to cease operations.</p>

        <p></p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">6</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><i>The market for our stock is limited and our stock price may be volatile.</i></p>
        <br>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">The market for our common stock has been limited due to low trading volume and the small number of brokerage firms acting as market makers. Because of the limitations of our market and volatility of the market price of our stock, investors may face difficulties in selling shares at attractive prices when they want to. The average daily trading volume for our stock has varied significantly
        from week to week and from month to month, and the trading volume often varies widely from day to day.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><i>Waste to Energy</i> <i>does not pay cash dividends.</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy does not pay cash dividends. We have not paid any cash dividends since inception and have no intention of paying any cash dividends in the foreseeable future. Any future dividends would be at the discretion of our board of directors and would depend on, among other things, future earnings, our operating and financial condition, our capital requirements, and general business
        conditions.&nbsp;Therefore, shareholders should not expect any type of cash flow from their investment.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><i>We incur significant expenses as a result of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, which expenses may continue to negatively impact our financial performance.</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">We incur significant legal, accounting and other expenses as a result of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, as well as related rules implemented by the Commission, which control the corporate governance practices of public companies. Compliance with these laws, rules and regulations, including compliance with Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, as discussed in the following risk
        factor, has substantially increased our expenses, including legal and accounting costs, and made some activities more time-consuming and costly. Further, expenses related to our compliance may increase in the future, as legislation affecting smaller reporting companies comes into effect that may negatively impact our financial performance to the point of having a material adverse effect on our results of operations and financial condition.</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><i>Our internal controls over financial reporting</i> <i>are</i> <i>not considered effective, which</i> <i>may</i> <i>result in a loss of investor confidence in our financial reports and in turn have an adverse effect on our stock price.</i></p>
        <br>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Pursuant to Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002 we are required to furnish a report by our management on our internal controls over financial reporting. Such report must contain, among other matters, an assessment of the effectiveness of our internal controls over financial reporting as of the end of the year, including a statement as to whether or not our internal controls over
        financial reporting are effective. This assessment must include disclosure of any material weaknesses in our internal controls over financial reporting identified by management. As we have been unable assert that our internal controls are fully effective at this time, investors may lose confidence in the accuracy and completeness of our financial reports, which in turn could cause our stock price to decline.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><i>Waste to Energy</i><i>&rsquo;s shareholders may face significant restrictions on their stock.</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy Group Inc.&rsquo;s stock differs from many stocks in that it is a &ldquo;penny stock.&rdquo; The Commission has adopted a number of rules to regulate &ldquo;penny stocks&rdquo; including, but not limited to, those rules from the Securities Act of 1933, as amended (&ldquo;Securities Act&rdquo;) as follows:</p>

        <p></p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">7</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">3a51-1&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which defines penny stock as, generally speaking, those securities which are not listed on either NASDAQ or a national securities exchange and are priced under $5, excluding securities of issuers that have net tangible assets greater than $2 million if they have been in operation at least three years, greater than $5 million if in operation less than three
        years, or average revenue of at least $6 million for the last three years;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -36px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.5in" align="left">15g-1&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which outlines transactions by broker/dealers which are exempt from 15g-2 through 15g-6 as those whose commissions from traders are lower than 5% total commissions;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -36px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.5in" align="left">15g-2&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which details that brokers must disclose risks of penny stock on Schedule 15G;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -36px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.5in" align="left">15g-3&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which details that broker/dealers must disclose quotes and other information relating to the penny stock market;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -27px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.4in" align="left">15g-4&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which explains that compensation of broker/dealers must be disclosed;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -36px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.5in" align="left">15g-5&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which explains that compensation of persons associated in connection with penny stock sales must be disclosed;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -27px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.4in" align="left">15g-6&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which outlines that broker/dealers must send out monthly account statements; and</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: -27px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0.4in" align="left">15g-9&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which defines sales practice requirements.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Since our securities constitute a &ldquo;penny stock&rdquo; within the meaning of the rules, the rules would apply to us and our securities. Because these rules provide regulatory burdens upon broker-dealers, they may affect the ability of shareholders to sell their securities in any market that may develop; the rules themselves may limit the market for penny stocks. Additionally, the market
        among dealers may not be active. Investors in penny stock often are unable to sell stock back to the dealer that sold them the stock. The mark-ups or commissions charged by the broker-dealers may be greater than any profit a seller may make. Because of large dealer spreads, investors may be unable to sell the stock immediately back to the dealer at the same price the dealer sold the stock to the investor. In some cases, the stock may fall quickly in value. Investors may be unable to
        reap any profit from any sale of the stock, if they can sell it at all.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Shareholders should be aware that, according to Commission Release No. 34-29093 dated April&nbsp;17, 1991, the market for penny stocks has suffered from patterns of fraud and abuse. These patterns include:</p>

        <p></p>

        <table style="FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman, Times, serif'; COLOR: black">
            <tr>
                <td>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'SYMBOL'; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; FONT-SIZE: 11pt">&middot;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">control of the market for the security by one or a few broker-dealers that are often related to the promoter or issuer;</p>
                </td>
            </tr>
        </table>
        <br>

        <table style="FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman, Times, serif'; COLOR: black">
            <tr>
                <td>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'SYMBOL'; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; FONT-SIZE: 11pt">&middot;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">manipulation of prices through prearranged matching of purchases and sales and false and misleading press releases;</td>
            </tr>
        </table>
        <br>

        <table style="FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman, Times, serif'; COLOR: black">
            <tr>
                <td>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'SYMBOL'; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; FONT-SIZE: 11pt">&middot;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">&ldquo;boiler room&rdquo; practices involving high pressure sales tactics and unrealistic price projections by inexperienced sales persons;</td>
            </tr>
        </table>
        <br>

        <table style="FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman, Times, serif'; COLOR: black">
            <tr>
                <td>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'SYMBOL'; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; FONT-SIZE: 11pt">&middot;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">excessive and undisclosed bid-ask differentials and mark-ups by selling broker-dealers; and</td>
            </tr>
        </table>
        <br>

        <table style="FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman, Times, serif'; COLOR: black">
            <tr>
                <td>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">
                    <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'SYMBOL'; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; FONT-SIZE: 11pt">&middot;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
                </td>

                <td valign="top">the wholesale dumping of the same securities by promoters and broker-dealers after prices have been manipulated to a desired level, along with the inevitable collapse of those prices with consequent investor losses.</td>
            </tr>
        </table>
        <br>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="justify"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt"><a name="A8"></a><a name="itemoneb">ITEM 1B.</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;UNRESOLVED STAFF COMMENTS</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="justify"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Not applicable.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Capital Stock</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">The following is a summary of the material terms of the Waste to Energy&rsquo;s capital stock. This summary is subject to and qualified by our articles of incorporation and bylaws.<br>
        </p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">9</a></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Common Stock</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">As of September 29, 2009 there were 38 shareholders of record holding a total of 50,265,000 shares of fully paid and non-assessable common stock of the 2,500,000,000 shares of common stock, par value $0.0001, authorized. The board of directors believes that the number of beneficial owners is greater than the number of record holders because a portion of our outstanding common stock is held in
        broker &ldquo;street names&rdquo; for the benefit of individual investors. The holders of the common stock are entitled to one vote for each share held of record on all matters submitted to a vote of stockholders. Holders of the common stock have no pre-emptive rights and no right to convert their common stock into any other securities. There are no redemption or sinking fund provisions applicable to the common stock.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Preferred Stock</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">As of September 29, 2009 there were no shares issued and outstanding of the 50,000,000 shares of preferred stock authorized. The par value of the preferred stock is $0.0001 per share. Waste to Energy&rsquo;s preferred stock may have such rights, preferences and designations and may be issued in such series as determined by the board of directors.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Dividends</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy has not declared any cash dividends since inception and does not anticipate paying any dividends in the near future. The payment of dividends is within the discretion of the board of directors and will depend on our earnings, capital requirements, financial condition, and other relevant factors. There are no restrictions that currently limit Waste to Energy&rsquo;s ability to
        pay dividends on its common stock other than those generally imposed by applicable state law.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Securities Authorized For Issuance under Equity Compensation Plans</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Waste to Energy had not approved any equity compensation plans as of September 29, 2009.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Warrants</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy had no warrants to purchase shares of its common stock outstanding as of September 29, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Stock Options</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy had no stock options to purchase shares of its common stock outstanding as of September 29, 2009 though it does intend to implement a Stock Option Plan during 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Convertible Securities</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy had no securities convertible into the shares of its common stock as of September 29, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Transfer Agent and Registrar</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Our transfer agent is Island Stock Transfer, located at 100 Second Avenue South, Suite 300, St. Petersburg, Florida, 33701. (727) 289-0010.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Recent Sales of Unregistered Securities; Use of Proceeds from Registered Securities</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy did not have any sale of unregistered securities during the fiscal year ended May 31, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Subsequent to the year ending May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy issued a Promissory Note in the amount of $50,000 to Austin Crook. Interest is accruing at the rate of 8% per annum. The proceeds of this loan were used to reduce our accounts payable.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Purchases of Equity Securities made by the Issuer and Affiliated Purchasers</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy has not repurchased any shares of its common stock during the fiscal year ended September 29, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><a name="A11"></a><a name="itemsix">ITEM 6. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SELECTED FINANCIAL DATA</a></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Not applicable.</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">&nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><a name="itemseven"></a></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">ITEM 7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;MANAGEMENT&rsquo;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL&nbsp;CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATION</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">This <i>Management&rsquo;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and</i> <i>Results of Operations</i> and other parts of this current report contain forward-looking statements that involve risks and uncertainties. Forward-looking statements can also be identified by words such as &ldquo;anticipates,&rdquo; &ldquo;expects,&rdquo; &ldquo;believes,&rdquo; &ldquo;plans,&rdquo;
        &ldquo;predicts,&rdquo; and similar terms. Forward-looking statements are not guarantees of future performance and our actual results may differ significantly from the results discussed in the forward-looking statements. Factors that might cause such differences include but are not limited to those discussed in the subsection entitled <i>Forward-Looking Statements and Factors That May Affect Future Results and Financial Condition</i> below. The following discussion should be read in
        conjunction with our financial statements and notes thereto included in this current report. Our fiscal year end is May 31.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="center"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Plan of Operation</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy&rsquo;s plan of operation for</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">the coming year is to identify and</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">acquire or</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">develop a revenue producing business through merger or acquisition.</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">We do not plan to limit our options to
        any particular industry, but will evaluate each opportunity on its merits.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">We have not yet entered into any agreement, nor do we have any commitment or understanding to enter into or become engaged in any transaction, as of the date of this filing.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy&rsquo;s plan of operation will require $100,000 in funding over the next</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">twelve</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">months. This funding is not currently available. Should we merge with or acquire a suitable business opportunity within the next</font>
        <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">twelve</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">months our funding requirements will change.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="center">Results of Operations</p>

        <p></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">During the year ended May 31, 2009, we abandoned an understanding to acquire Waste to Energy Group, LLC and have since resumed the process of identifying a prospective business opportunity for merger or acquisition.<br>
        </p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">11</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">has been funded since inception through private debt or equity placements or by major shareholders in the form of loans. All of the capital raised to date has been allocated for general and administrative costs, exploration expenses, loans and interest expenses.</font></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="center">&nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">We do not expect to receive revenues within the next twelve months of operation or ever, since we have yet to acquire a business opportunity, which opportunity if acquired, may or may not produce revenue.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="justify"><i>Net Income/Losses</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">For the period from inception until May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy incurred net losses of $411,434. Net losses for the year ended May 31, 2009 were $354,363 as compared to $28,993 for the year ended May 31, 2008. The increase in net losses over the comparative periods can be attributed to our investment in Waste to Energy Group LLC (that was written off), an increase in consulting and
        professional fees associated to that transaction and costs associated with doing due diligence on other investment opportunities. We will likely continue to operate at a loss through fiscal 2010 and due to the nature of Waste to Energy Group&rsquo;s research and development operations cannot determine whether we will ever generate revenues from operations.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Operating</i> <i>Expenses</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Operating expenses for the year ended May 31, 2009 were $344,034 as compared to $31,166 for the year ended May 31, 2008. The increase in operating expenses is primarily due to increased administrative and professional fees and our investment in Waste to Energy Group LLC. Operating expenses included accounting costs, consulting fees, employment costs, costs associated with the preparation of
        disclosure documentation and the impairment of our investment.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Income Tax Expense (Benefit)</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy may have a prospective income tax benefit resulting from a net operating loss carry-forward and start up costs that will offset any future operating profit.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Impact of Inflation</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Waste to Energy believes that inflation has not had a material effect on operations for the period from June 27, 2006 (inception) to May 31, 2009.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Capital Expenditures</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Waste to Energy has not spent significant amounts of capital for the period from June 27, 2006 (inception) to May 31, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Liquidity and Capital Resources</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy has been in the development stage since inception. At May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy had a working capital deficit of $344,089 and current assets of $15 comprised of cash on hand and total assets of $15,862 comprised of computer equipment and, a website. At May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy had liabilities of $344,104 consisting of accounts payable and accruals, loans payable,
        accrued interest on loans payable, loans payable to related party and accrued interest on loans from related party. Stockholders deficit in Waste to Energy was $328,242 as of May 31, 2009.</p>

        <div style="MARGIN-TOP: 12pt" title="EE+ Page Footer">
            <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="center"><a name="PAGENUM">12</a></p>
        </div>
        <!-- PAGE BREAK  --><a href="#TableOfContents">Return to Table of Contents</a>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">For the period from inception until May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy&rsquo;s cash flow used in operating activities was $298,423. Cash flows used in operating activities for the year ended May 31, 2009 were $247,964 compared to $22,380 for the year ended May 31, 2008. The cash flow used in operating activities during the current period was due to net losses and adjustments from an increase in
        accounts payable, accrued interest on loans and an accounts receivable outstanding from the year ending May 31, 2008.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">For the period from inception until May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy&rsquo;s cash flow used investing activities was $29,462. Cash flow used in investing activities for the year ended May 31, 2009 were $2,465 as compared to $26,997 for the year ended May 31, 2008.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">For the period from inception until May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy&rsquo;s cash flow provided by financing activities was $327,900. Cash flow provided by financing activities for the year ended May 31, 2009 was $249,758 as compared to $0 for the year ended May 31, 2008. Cash flows provided by financing activities can be primarily attributed to loans.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">Waste to Energy had no lines of credit or other bank financing arrangements as of May 31, 2009.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy does not expect to pay cash dividends in the foreseeable future.<br>
        <br>
        Waste to Energy has no defined benefit plan or contractual commitment with any of its officers or directors.<br>
        <br>
        Waste to Energy has no current plans for any significant purchase or sale of any plant or equipment.<br>
        <br>
        Waste to Energy has no current plans to make any changes in the number of employees.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Off Balance Sheet Arrangements</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">As of May 31, 2009 Waste to Energy had no off-balance sheet arrangements that have or are reasonably likely to have a current or future effect on our financial condition, changes in financial condition, revenues or expenses, results of operations, liquidity, capital expenditures, or capital resources that is material to stockholders.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Going Concern</i><br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">Our auditors have expressed an opinion as to Waste to Energy&rsquo;s ability to continue as a going concern as a result of net losses of $411,434 as of May 31, 2009. Waste to Energy&rsquo;s ability to continue as a going concern is subject to the ability of Waste to Energy to realize a profit and /or obtain funding from outside sources. Management&rsquo;s plan to address Waste to
        Energy&rsquo;s ability to continue as a going concern includes: (i) obtaining funding from the private placement of debt or equity; (ii) realizing revenues from the commercialization of a business opportunity; and (iii) obtaining loans and grants from financial or government institutions. Management believes that it will be able to obtain funding to allow Waste to Energy to remain a going concern through the methods discussed above, though there can be no assurances that such methods
        will prove successful.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><i>Critical Accounting Policies</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">In the notes to the audited financial statements for</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">the year ended</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">May 31, 2009</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">included in this</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Form 10-K, Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">discusses those accounting policies
        that are considered to be significant in determining the results of operations and our</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">financial position. Waste to Energy</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">believes that the accounting principles utilized by</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">us</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">conform to accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">The preparation of financial statements requires management to make significant estimates and judgments that affect the reported amounts of assets, liabilities, revenues and expenses. By their nature, these judgments are subject to an inherent degree of uncertainty. On an on-going</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">basis, Waste to Energy</font>
        <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">evaluates our</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">estimates, including those related to bad debts, inventories, intangible assets, warranty obligations, product liability, revenue, and income taxes. We base our</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">estimates on historical experience and other facts and circumstances that are believed to be reasonable, and the results form the basis for making judgments about the carrying value of assets and liabilities. The
        actual results may differ from these estimates under different assumptions or conditions.</font></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><i><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Stock-Based Compensation</font></i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold" align="left"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt; FONT-WEIGHT: normal">We have adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board</font> <font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt; FONT-WEIGHT: normal">(&ldquo;FASB&rdquo;) No. 123 (revised 2004) (Statements of Financial Accounting Standards (&ldquo;SFAS&rdquo;) No. 123R), Share-Based Payment, which addresses the accounting for stock-based payment
        transactions in which an enterprise receives employee services in exchange for (a) equity instruments of the enterprise or (b) liabilities that are based on the fair value of the enterprise&rsquo;s equity instruments or that may be settled by the issuance of such equity instruments. </font></p>

        </div>

        <div style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%; HEIGHT: 1px; FONT-SIZE: 1pt" title="EE+ Page Break">
            <hr width="100%">
        </div>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt; FONT-WEIGHT: bold" align="left"><b><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt; FONT-WEIGHT: normal">We account for equity instruments issued in exchange for the receipt of goods or services from other than employees in accordance with SFAS No. 123 and the conclusions reached by the Emerging Issues Task Force (&ldquo;EITF&rdquo;) in Issue No. 96-18. Costs are measured at the estimated fair market value
        of the consideration received or the estimated fair value of the equity instruments issued, whichever is more reliably measurable. The value of equity instruments issued for consideration other than employee services is determined on the earliest of a performance commitment or completion of performance by the provider of goods or services as defined by EITF 96-18.</font></b></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 12pt" align="left"><i><font style="FONT-SIZE: 11pt">Recent Accounting Pronouncements</font></i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in; FONT-SIZE: 11pt" align="left">In June 2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 165, &ldquo;Subsequent Events,&rdquo; (&ldquo;SFAS No. 165&rdquo;). SFAS 165 establishes general standards of accounting for and disclosure of events that occur after the balance sheet date but before financial statements are issued or are available to be issued. SFAS 165 applies to both interim
        financial statements and annual financial statements. SFAS 165 is effective for interim or annual financial periods ending after June 15, 2009. SFAS 165 does not have a material impact on our financial statements.<br>
        <br>
        In June&nbsp;2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;166, &ldquo;Accounting for Transfers of Financial Assets, an amendment to SFAS No.&nbsp;140,&rdquo; (&ldquo;SFAS 166&rdquo;). SFAS 166 eliminates the concept of a &ldquo;qualifying special-purpose entity,&rdquo; changes the requirements for derecognizing financial assets, and requires additional disclosures in order to enhance information reported to users of financial statements by providing greater
        transparency about transfers of financial assets, including securitization transactions, and an entity&rsquo;s continuing involvement in and exposure to the risks related to transferred financial assets. SFAS 166 is effective for fiscal years beginning after November&nbsp;15, 2009.&nbsp;Waste to Energy will adopt SFAS&nbsp;166 in fiscal 2010. Waste to Energy does not expect that the adoption of SFAS 166 will have a material impact on the financial statements.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 8.3pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left">In June 2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 167, &ldquo;Amendments to FASB Interpretation No. 46(R),&rdquo; (&ldquo;SFAS 167&rdquo;). The amendments include: (1) the elimination of the exemption for qualifying special purpose entities, (2) a new approach for determining who should consolidate a variable-interest entity, and (3) changes to when it is
        necessary to reassess who should consolidate a variable-interest entity. SFAS 167 is effective for the first annual reporting period beginning after November 15, 2009 and for interim periods within that first annual reporting period. Waste to Energy will adopt SFAS 167 in fiscal 2010. Waste to Energy does not expect that the adoption of SFAS 167 will have a material impact on the financial statements.<br>
        <br>
        In June 2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;168, &ldquo;The FASB Accounting Standards Codification and the Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles,&rdquo; (&ldquo;SFAS 168&rdquo;). SFAS 168 replaces FASB Statement No.&nbsp;162, &ldquo;The Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles&rdquo;, and establishes the FASB Accounting Standards Codification (&ldquo;Codification&rdquo;) as the source of authoritative accounting
        principles recognized by the FASB to be applied by nongovernmental entities in the preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles (&ldquo;GAAP&rdquo;). SFAS 168 is effective for interim and annual periods ending after September&nbsp;15, 2009. Waste to Energy will begin to use the new Codification when referring to GAAP in its annual report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ending December 31, 2009. This will not have an impact on the
        results of Waste to Energy.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="left"><a name="A15"></a><a name="itemsevena">ITEM 7 A.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;QUANTITATIVE AND QUALITATIVE DISCLOSURES ABOUT MARKET RISK</a><br>
        <br>
        Not required.</p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><a name="itemeight"></a></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="center"><b><u>REPORT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM</u></b></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify"><b>To the Board of Directors<br>
        Waste to Energy Group, Inc. (formerly Your Digital Memories, Inc.)<br>
        (A Development Stage Company)</b></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="MARGIN-TOP: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN-BOTTOM: 0pt; MARGIN-LEFT: 0in" align="justify">We have audited the accompanying balance sheets of Waste to Energy Group, Inc. (A Development Stage Company) as of May 31, 2009 and 2008, and the related statements of operations, stockholders&rsquo; equity (deficit) and cash flows for the years ended May 31, 2009, 2008 and since inception on June 27, 2006 through May 31, 2009. These financial statements are the responsibility of the
        Company&rsquo;s management. Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits.<br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        We conduct our audits in accordance with standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (United States). Those standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant
        estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.<br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of Waste to Energy Group, Inc. (A Development Stage Company) as of May 31, 2009 and 2008, and the related statements of operations, stockholders&rsquo; equity (deficit) and cash flows for the years ended May 31, 2009, 2008 and since inception on June 27, 2006 through May 31, 2009, in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of
        America.<br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        The accompanying financial statements have been prepared assuming that the Company will continue as a going concern. As discussed in Note 8 to the financial statements, the Company has had net losses of $411,434 since inception, which raises substantial doubt about its ability to continue as a going concern. Management&rsquo;s plans concerning these matters are also described in Note 8. The financial statements do not include any adjustments that might result from the outcome of this
        uncertainty.</p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left"><u>Note 1 &ndash; General Organization and Business</u></p>

        <p></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy Group, Inc. (the &ldquo;Company&rdquo;) was incorporated in the state of Nevada on June 27, 2006.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Waste to Energy Group Inc., a wholly-owned subsidiary of Your Digital Memories Inc., was incorporated in the state of Nevada on August 13, 2008. Waste to Energy Group Inc. and Your Digital Memories Inc. entered into an Agreement and Plan of Merger on August 14, 2008. The board of directors of Waste to Energy Group Inc. and Your Digital Memories Inc. deemed it advisable and in the best interest of their respective
        companies and shareholders that Waste to Energy be merged with and into Your Digital Memories Inc. with Your Digital Memories Inc. remaining as the surviving corporation under the name Waste to Energy Group Inc.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><u>Note 2 &ndash; Significant Accounting Policies</u></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Accounting Basis</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">These financial statements are prepared on the accrual basis of accounting in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Cash and Cash Equivalents<br>
        &nbsp;</i></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify">For the purposes of the statement of cash flows, cash flows include all highly liquid investments with a maturity of three months or less.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Financial Instrument<br>
        &nbsp;</i></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify">The Company's financial instruments consist of Promissory Notes for loans made to the Company.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Some of the amounts due to the note holders are non interest-bearing. It is management's opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency or credit risks arising from its other financial instruments and that their fair values approximate their carrying values except where separately disclosed.</p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><u>Note 2 &ndash; Significant Accounting Policies &ndash; cont.</u></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Use of Estimates</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">The preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles of the United States requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the year. The more significant areas
        requiring the use of estimates include asset impairment, stock-based compensation, and future income tax amounts. Management bases its estimates on historical experience and on other assumptions considered to be reasonable under the circumstances. However, actual results may differ from the estimates.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Loss Per Share</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Net income (loss) per common share is computed based on the weighted average number of common shares outstanding and common stock equivalents, if not anti-dilutive. The Company has not issued any potentially dilutive common shares.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Basic loss per share is calculated using the weighted average number of common shares outstanding and the treasury stock method is used to calculate diluted earnings per share. For the years presented, this calculation proved to be anti-dilutive.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify"><i>Dividends<br>
        &nbsp;</i></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">The Company has not adopted any policy regarding payment of dividends. No dividends have been paid during the period shown.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left"><i>Advertising Costs</i></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">The Company will expense its advertising costs when incurred. There have been no expenditures on advertising since inception.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">The Company has 2,500,000,000 common shares authorized at a par value of $0.0001 per share and 50,000,000 shares of preferred stock, par value $0.0001 per share. All common stock shares have equal voting rights, are non-assessable and have one vote per share. Voting rights are not cumulative and, therefore, the holders of more than 50% of the common stock could, if they choose to do so, elect all the directors of the
        Company.<br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        Common Shares &ndash; Issued and Outstanding<br>
        &nbsp;<br>
        On June 27, 2006 (inception), the Company issued 2,500,000 shares of its common stock to a director for cash consideration of $100.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">On September 13, 2006, the Company issued 62,500,000 shares of its common stock to a director for cash consideration of $2,500.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">On October 31, 2006, the Company issued 125,300,000 shares of its common stock to a director for cash consideration of $5,012.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">On April 30, 2007, the Company completed a private placement for 35,265,000 common shares at $0.002 per share for total consideration of $70,530.</p>

        <p></p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="justify">As of May 31, 2009, the Company had 50,265,000 common shares issued and outstanding.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">During the year ending May 31, 2009, 175,300,000 shares were voluntarily cancelled, subsequent to which cancellation there were 225,565,000 common shares of the Company issued and outstanding.<br>
        &nbsp;</p>

        <p style="TEXT-INDENT: 0px; MARGIN: 0pt 0.1in 0pt 0in" align="left">Subsequent to the share cancellation the Company authorized to effect a forward split of the Company&rsquo;s stock on a 25 new for 1 old basis, such that its authorized capital shall increase from 100,000,000 shares of common stock with a par value of $0.0001 to 2,500,000,000 shares of common stock with a par value of $0.0001 and, correspondingly, its issued and outstanding shares of common stock shall decrease from
        225,565,000 shares of common stock to 50,265,000 shares of common stock. The effective date for the forward stock split was September 3, 2008. The forward split caused a mandatory exchange of share certificates. The forward split was retroactively applied to the Statement of Stockholders&rsquo; Equity.</p>

The terms of the consulting agreement are $5,000 per month payable in consulting fees and reimbursement to the consultant for all reasonable business expenses incurred by it in the performance of its duties.</p>
